private[network] case class DelayedCloseSocket(socket: SocketChannel, endThrottleTimeMs: Long) extends Ordered[DelayedCloseSocket] {\n555:     override def compare(that: DelayedCloseSocket): Int = Remove them from the processor list first so that no more\n560:     // connections are assigned. Shutdown the removed processors, closing the selector and its connections.\n561:     // The processors are then removed from `requestChannel` and any pending responses to these processors are dropped.\n562:     val toRemove = processors.takeRight(removeCount)\n563:     processors.remove(processors.size - removeCount, removeCount)\n564:     toRemove.foreach(_.close())\n565:     toRemove.foreach(processor => requestChannel.removeProcessor(processor.id))\n566:   }\n567: \n568:   def beginShutdown(): Unit = {\n569:     if (shouldRun.getAndSet(false)) {\n570:       wakeup()\n571:       synchronized {\n572:         processors.foreach(_.beginShutdown())\n573:       }\n574:     }\n575:   }\n576: \n577:   def close(): Unit = {\n578:     beginShutdown()\n579:     thread.join()\n580:     if (!started.get) {\n581:       closeAll()\n582:     }\n583:     synchronized {\n584:       processors.foreach(_.close())\n585:     }\n586:   }\n587: \n588:   /**\n589:    * Accept loop that checks for new connection attempts\n590:    */\n591:   override def run(): Unit = {\n592:     serverChannel.register(nioSelector, SelectionKey.OP_ACCEPT)\n593:     try {\n594:       while (shouldRun.get()) {\n595:         try {\n596:           acceptNewConnections()\n597:           closeThrottledConnections()\n598:         }\n599:         catch {\n600:           // We catch all the throwables to prevent the acceptor thread from exiting on exceptions due\n601:           // to a select operation on a specific channel or a bad request. We don't want\n602:           // the broker to stop responding to requests from other clients in these scenarios.\n603:           case e: ControlThrowable => throw e\n604:           case e: Throwable => error(\"Error occurred\", e)\n605:         }\n606:       }\n607:     } finally {\n608:       closeAll()\n609:     }\n610:   }\n611: \n612:   private def closeAll(): Unit = {\n613: throttledSockets.clear()\n619:   }\n620: \n621:   /**\n622:    * Create a server socket to listen for connections on.\n623:    */\n624:   private def openServerSocket(host: String, port: Int, }\n638: \n639:   /**\n640:    * Listen for new connections and assign accepted connections to processors using round-robin.\n641:    */\n642:   private def acceptNewConnections(): Unit = {\n643: */\n1153:   def accept(socketChannel: SocketChannel,\n1154:              mayBlock: Boolean,\n1155:              acceptorBlockedPercentMeter: com.yammer.metrics.core.Meter): Boolean = {\n1156:     val \"clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/NetworkSend.java\", \"symbol\": \"NetworkSend\"}\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"## Kafka Network Layer Architecture\\n\\nThe Apache Kafka network layer is implemented across multiple components spanning both server-side (Scala) and common/client-side (Java) code. The architecture follows a multi-threaded, NIO-based design:\\n\\n### Server-Side Components (Scala)\\n\\n**SocketServer (core/src/main/scala/kafka/network/SocketServer.scala)**: The main orchestrator of the network layer. It manages:\\n- DataPlaneAcceptor threads that accept incoming client connections\\n- Processor threads that handle I/O operations for accepted connections\\n- Integration with RequestChannel for request/response handoff\\n- Configuration and lifecycle management of network listeners\\n\\n**DataPlaneAcceptor (core/src/main/scala/kafka/network/SocketServer.scala)**: Handles accepting new client connections on a specified endpoint. One Acceptor thread per listener is spawned, and it:\\n- Listens on a ServerSocket for incoming connections\\n- Creates new SocketChannel instances when connections arrive\\n- Assigns accepted connections to Processor threads in round-robin fashion\\n\\n**Processor (core/src/main/scala/kafka/network/SocketServer.scala)**: Worker threads that handle I/O for multiple connections. Each Processor:\\n- Maintains its own NIO Selector for polling multiple connections\\n- Reads incoming requests from KafkaChannels\\n- Receives responses from RequestChannel and writes them to clients\\n- Manages connection state and metrics\\n- Runs in a loop: poll selector → process completed receives → send responses\\n\\n**RequestChannel (core/src/main/scala/kafka/network/RequestChannel.scala)**: The handoff point between network and request handling layers. It:\\n- Receives parsed Request objects from Processor threads\\n- Routes requests to handler threads\\n- Receives Response objects from handlers and queues them back to Processors\\n- Manages request/response queuing and metrics\\n- Supports per-processor response queues\\n\\n**Request (core/src/main/scala/kafka/network/RequestChannel.scala)**: Encapsulates a single request with:\\n- Parser-extracted request body\\n- RequestContext with protocol information\\n- Timing information for metrics\\n- Memory pool allocations\\n- Envelope support for inter-broker forwarding\\n\\n### Common/Client-Side NIO Components (Java)\\n\\n**Selector (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/Selector.java)**: The core NIO-based multiplexer implementing the Selectable interface:\\n- Uses java.nio.channels.Selector for non-blocking I/O\\n- Manages multiple KafkaChannel instances\\n- Provides poll() method that selects ready channels and processes I/O\\n- Maintains lists of completedReceives and completedSends\\n- Handles connection state transitions and metrics\\n- Thread-unsafe (single-threaded usage per instance)\\n\\n**KafkaChannel (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/KafkaChannel.java)**: Represents a single network connection:\\n- Wraps a SocketChannel and TransportLayer\\n- Manages current NetworkReceive and NetworkSend objects\\n- Handles authentication state and re-authentication\\n- Provides read() and write() methods for I/O operations\\n- Tracks connection state (CONNECTING, READY, AUTHENTICATING, etc.)\\n- Supports muting/unmuting for flow control\\n\\n**NetworkReceive (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/NetworkReceive.java)**: Manages incoming message bytes:\\n- Reads size-delimited messages from the network\\n- Uses MemoryPool for buffer allocation\\n- Handles partial receives across multiple read() calls\\n- Exposes payload() ByteBuffer once complete\\n- Supports implemented across multiple components spanning both server-side (Scala) and common/client-side (Java) code. The architecture follows a multi-threaded, NIO-based design:\\n\\n### Server-Side Components (Scala)\\n\\n**SocketServer (core/src/main/scala/kafka/network/SocketServer.scala)**: The main orchestrator of the network layer. It manages:\\n- DataPlaneAcceptor threads that accept incoming client connections\\n- Processor threads that handle I/O operations for accepted connections\\n- Integration with RequestChannel for request/response handoff\\n- Configuration and lifecycle management of network listeners\\n\\n**DataPlaneAcceptor (core/src/main/scala/kafka/network/SocketServer.scala)**: Handles accepting new client connections on a specified endpoint. One Acceptor thread per listener is spawned, and it:\\n- Listens on a ServerSocket for incoming connections\\n- Creates new SocketChannel instances when connections arrive\\n- Assigns accepted connections to Processor threads in round-robin fashion\\n\\n**Processor (core/src/main/scala/kafka/network/SocketServer.scala)**: Worker threads that handle I/O for multiple connections. Each Processor:\\n- Maintains its own NIO Selector for polling multiple connections\\n- Reads incoming requests from KafkaChannels\\n- Receives responses from RequestChannel and writes them to clients\\n- Manages connection state and metrics\\n- Runs in a loop: poll selector → process completed receives → send responses\\n\\n**RequestChannel (core/src/main/scala/kafka/network/RequestChannel.scala)**: The handoff point between network and request handling layers. It:\\n- Receives parsed Request objects from Processor threads\\n- Routes requests to handler threads\\n- Receives Response objects from handlers and queues them back to Processors\\n- Manages request/response queuing and metrics\\n- Supports per-processor response queues\\n\\n**Request (core/src/main/scala/kafka/network/RequestChannel.scala)**: Encapsulates a single request with:\\n- Parser-extracted request body\\n- RequestContext with protocol information\\n- Timing information for metrics\\n- Memory pool allocations\\n- Envelope support for inter-broker forwarding\\n\\n### Common/Client-Side NIO Components (Java)\\n\\n**Selector (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/Selector.java)**: The core NIO-based multiplexer implementing the Selectable interface:\\n- Uses java.nio.channels.Selector for non-blocking I/O\\n- Manages multiple KafkaChannel instances\\n- Provides poll() method that selects ready channels and processes I/O\\n- Maintains lists of completedReceives and completedSends\\n- Handles connection state transitions and metrics\\n- Thread-unsafe (single-threaded usage per instance)\\n\\n**KafkaChannel (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/KafkaChannel.java)**: Represents a single network connection:\\n- Wraps a SocketChannel and TransportLayer\\n- Manages current NetworkReceive and NetworkSend objects\\n- Handles authentication state and re-authentication\\n- Provides read() and write() methods for I/O operations\\n- Tracks connection state (CONNECTING, READY, AUTHENTICATING, etc.)\\n- Supports muting/unmuting for flow control\\n\\n**NetworkReceive (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/NetworkReceive.java)**: Manages incoming message bytes:\\n- Reads size-delimited messages from the network\\n- Uses MemoryPool for buffer allocation\\n- Handles partial receives across multiple read() calls\\n- Exposes payload() ByteBuffer once complete\\n- Supports unlimited or bounded size limits\\n\\n**NetworkSend (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/NetworkSend.java)**: Wrapper around outgoing messages:\\n- Holds destination connection ID\\n- Wraps a Send implementation (e.g., ByteBufferSend)\\n- Supports size-prefixed message format\\n\\n**ByteBufferSend (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/ByteBufferSend.java)**: Concrete Send implementation for ByteBuffer arrays:\\n- Writes multiple ByteBuffers with size prefix\\n- Supports scatter-gather I/O\\n- Implements Send interface for polymorphic use\\n\\n### Receive.java)**: Generic interfaces for message I/O:\\n- Send defines writeTo() for sending data\\n- Receive defines readFrom() for reading data\\n- NetworkSend and NetworkReceive implement these\\n\\n**TransportLayer (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/TransportLayer.java)**: Interface for protocol-specific transport:\\n- Abstracts SSL/SASL/plaintext differences\\n- creating KafkaChannel instances:\\n- Creates TransportLayer based on security protocol\\n- Configures authenticators (SASL, SSL)\\n- Supports different modes (CLIENT, SERVER)\\n\\n### Security/Authentication Components\\n\\n**PlaintextChannelBuilder/TransportLayer**: No security, direct socket I/O\\n\\n**SslChannelBuilder/SslTransportLayer**: SSL/TLS encryption and certificates\\n\\n**SaslChannelBuilder**: SASL authentication mechanism support\\n\\n### Supporting Components\\n\\n**ChannelMetadataRegistry**: Tracks channel-specific
